Mr HA:WKE (Wills) (10.10)-1 take this opportunity of exposing the fact that this House earlier today was sUbjected to gross misrepresentation by, the Minister for Employment and Youth Affairs (Mr N. A. Brown). Apparently there is something endemic in this portfolio. Honourable members will recall that the previous oc~upant, after cross examination and investigation from this side of the House, had to concede that he had been guilty of misleading the House. Today I pu~ to the House in the debate on the matter of public importance that 55,000 young people in Australia in the last year had enjoyed the benefits of the Community Youth Support Scheme. I said that the attempt by the Government to explain away and justify its decision to discontinue the program was that more than enough additional programs would be provided under the Special Youth Employment Training Program and other manpower and training programs that would take up the 55,000 people.
The argument was clearly put. One would have thought that even the Minister could have understood it. He replied that I had come up with some imaginary figures. He did not know where I had got them. I got those figures from the Minister's own Department and publications. In particular, they came from the publication that was put out on Budget day by the Minister. It was headed Big Increases for Manpower and Training Programs'. It stated:
. . . 235,000 people-a record number-would be assisted by the Government's manpower and training programs in 1981-82, 23,000 more than 1980-81. The great majority would be young people.
In other words, in his own publication he stated that the additional number of new positions from the new expenditure would total 23,000. He conceded that only a portion would be additional new places for young people. The Minister also told the House that there would be approximately 70,000 new training places. His own statement released on Budget day said that at the most there will be 23,000 new places and ofthose only about 20,000 will be available for youth. How can the Minister justify talking in this House about the 70,000 new training places when his own news release stated that the absolute increase will be 23,000 and at the most 20,000 new places will be available for young people?
The situation is quite clearly exposed by the Minister's own Press release on 18 August. He has misled this House. There will not be 70,000 new places. At the most there will be 20,000. In 1980-81, 55,000 young Australians took advantage of the CYSS program. Simple arithmetic shows that in terms of coping with the continual

flow of new people into training programs, having looked after them, as a result of the Government's Budget decision, only 20,000 new places at the very most will be available. Therefore, 20,000 out of the 55,000 who have used CYSS will have the opportunity of taking up new places. This leaves a balance of over 30,000 who have been discarded by this Government in the abandonment of the CYSS program. Is it any wonder in those circumstances that in the Launceston Examiner of 22 August the following statement was made:

The 19 Community Youth Support Schemes in Tasmania are being wound up, contrary to a promise made last month by the Minister for Employment and Youth Affairs, Mr Brown.

I quoted from the Advertiser of June which

showed that the Minister deliberately

misrepresented the CYSS program in South

Australia.

.

The Examiner on 22 August, four days after the Budget, stated that contrary to the Minister's promise the 19 community youth support schemes in Tasmania are being broken up. The Minister has misled the House, either deliberately or through gross incompetence. On either ground he should, with any decency, tender his resignation to this House.

Mrs CHILD (Henty) (1O.15)-It is clearly obvious that in the tertiary sector the Government wants to reduce the .number of student places available. What else can be behind the decision of the razor gang to eliminate 30 colleges of advanced education? The Tertiary Education Commission has said that there is a need to transfer some of the student places in teacher education to new areas such as business studies and technologies but clearly this Government intends to go much further. The Government has a manic determination to discipline schools and the people who work in them. Some of us thought and all of us hoped that the Liberals' attack on schools was simply part of a passing phase as they discovered new villains to take the responsibility for their increasing high rate of youth unemployment. It is obviously the view of the Prime Minister (Mr Malcolm Fraser) that young school leavers lack the personal qualities and basic skills which confer employability upon them. If only the schools would do their part in correcting these deficien-
cies, the problem of youth unemployment would vanish, accordingto the Prime Minister.

The Minister for Employment and Youth Affairs (Mr N. A. Brown) continues totell us that there are plenty of jobs available if only the young will go to some of his training courses and then get out and look for them. There are nojobs, as we know, but the Government will not admit that it

752 REPRESENTATIVES 25 August 1981

Adjournment

presides over the worst unemployment this country has ever experienced. I point out to Government members that education is not simply about learning to get a job. It is also about learning how to live. The Government seems to have ignored much of the advice given by the Tertiary Education Commission and has twisted and deliberately misinterpreted other parts of this advice. The Government sees inefficiency where it
does not exist. It makes unsubstantiated accusations and decisions which are quite contrary to the evidence in the reports of the Tertiary Education Commission. The Government appears to know nothing or at least care nothing about the notion of investing in human capital as a resource for the future. I will speak specifically about the decision by the razor gang to force an amalgamation on Melbourne State College. Perhaps the Government does not know that the College was formed by an amalgamation. It was formed by the consolidation of the former Melbourne teachers' college which prepared the primary teachers, the secondary teachers' college and Kay House in which
teachers of secondary arts and crafts were prepared. Teacher education has continued at Melbourne State College for over 100 years. It is a large multi-disciplinary college. It teachers major studies in more areas of the creative arts, liberal arts, business studies and science than most other Victorian colleges of advanced education. It should continue to be funded as an autonomous institution with its own governing body. The range and mix of courses currently available at Melbourne State College provide a high degree of flexibility within teacher education and allow

ready response to changing needs for specific types of teachers. There is already on the college staff the expertise to extend this flexibility to professions related to teaching. All that is required is the recognition of a general studies degree. In the ad hoc approach taken by the Minister for Education (Mr Fife) towards getting rid of 30 colleges of advanced education, he has lost sight of the fact that it is essential that additional time is made available for proper consideration of amalgamations and possible alternatives. The Australian Council for Educational Research is currently investigating the educational needs of the western suburbs of Melbourne. Action should not be taken which could affect the ability of Melbourne State 'College to help meet these needs. Action should not be taken against Melbourne State College which could in any way deprive students who have already embarked on courses there.

Mr CAMPBELL (KalgoorIie) (10.20)-Mr Deputy Speaker, as you know, I represent a very large country electorate. It is an electorate from which comes a very large percentage of the wealth which honourable members opposite are always so ecstatic about. It is interesting to reflect on how the people living in this isolated area have been treated by this Government in this worst of all Budgets. The other day I had a representation from a constituent who lives 300 miles from KalgoorIie in an isolated area. Two and a half weeks ago this gentleman bought a motor vehicle in KalgoorIie. When one lives in such isolated conditions one does not buy a motor vehicle off the shelf. One has to get it sent up from the capital city. This is just one of the prices we pay for living in isolation.
The gentleman paid a very substantial deposit on the vehicle and returned to the bush. He came into Kalgoorlie one day after the Budget to find that his vehicle now would cost him almost $300 more than he had intended to pay for it. That is the sort of recognition given by this Government to, and one of the rewards bestowed by this Government on, people working in isolated areas and winning the wealth which this Government prizes so highly. Country people, of course, are affected in another way. Because this Government applies sales tax to the freight component, country people pay far more than people living in the city. It is the policy of the Australian Labor Party to discount the freight component from sales tax calculations. But this Government is notorious for the way in which it disregards the interests of country people.

Adjournment

25 August 1981 REPRESENTATIVES 753

This Government also prides itself on its help to the mining industry. What has it done? It has now levied a 17.S per cent tax on the construction of private railways. In this country private railways are constructed almost entirely by mining companies, and they are the ones affected by this tax. When we'look at the increased cost we can see that it is not just a straight 17.5 per cent; they are payirig 17.5 per cent on rolling stock, on locomotives, on railway lines and on railway sleepers-a tremendous cost. I do not know whether the Government would even be aware of the cost of transporting concrete railway sleepers over the distances involved. This Government also introduced a sales tax on vehicles used in the mining industry. They are mainly four-wheel drive vehicles, off-road vehicles or vehicles with high ground clearance which are essential for winning the wealth that this country needs. There was no attempt to tax four-wheel drive vehicles used in primary industry although in many cases their use is not warranted. But in the mining industry the Government has seen fit to impose this sudden 17.5 per cent slug. It certainly is a strange way to show appreciation of and regard for an industry which this Government purports to support. .
We see also in the Budget under the heading 'Anomalies' a sudden increase in the sales tax on such things as dog food. There will now be sales tax of 17.5 per cent on dog food. Does the Government realise what this is going to do in terms of raising the. cost of living for a lot of people in remote areas-a lot of pensioners who actually eat the stuff? It is going to impose on these people a significant reduction in their standard of living-they will no longer be able to enjoy the luxury of the dog food which they have been forced to buy by this highest taxing Government of all time. I would like to reflect on how anomalous it is that the Government can impose quite arbitrarily these taxes which clearly are going to penalise country people far more than city people. It is a disproportionate and unfair tax, and it is a thing to which the Government should give very serious consideration. If honourable members opposite want people to live and work ih the country, to fuel the resources boom that they are always talking about, they have to be prepared to do something for them. I suggest to them that this Budget is going to do nothing at all.
Mr BAUME (Macarthur) (10.25)-1 commend the expressions of concern and the feelings of distress that some members of the Opposition have expressed in relation to the Community Youth Support Scheme. I commend them for their newfound interest in the scheme now that it

is about to end. But I say with sincerity that the concern for many of the younger people who have been receiving a degree of benefit from CYSS is not exclusive to their side of the House. The issue seems to me to be: How will that money best be spent for the benefit of young people in Australia? ' It seems incontrovertible that there is a better prospect of doing things that are useful for the young people of Australia through the job support schemes which were introduced after CYSS was introduced than in fact by maintaining CYSS. The 60-odd per cent increase in the schemes going to assist young unemployed people to obtain prior work experience, practical job skills or otherwise prepare them for employment is a far more tangible and effective way of improving the lot of young people than CYSS unfortunately turned out to be.
However, I must say that there is a small group of people who were assisted by CYSS and who will not ?e in a position to be picked up by the other work training schemes which will in general be a far better and more sensible way to spend the money. This small group of people are those who are not in a situation in which they are capable of getting the benefit of pre-training schemes and in effect need some sort of pre-pre-training scheme or some kind of social support rather than the schemes which were provided for them at the periphery of CYSS. It seems to me to be important for honourable members opposite to recognise that that is the area of real need. To talk about maintaining CYSS in its old form while there are -these other much better programs seems to me to be missing the point entirely. I simply hope that the Government will be able to find an appropriate program-CYSS, I think, tended to be inappropriate-to pick up the small number of people from the CYSS program who will not be coped with under the work training schemes. Of course, most will be picked up by these excellent work training schemes. I heard from the honourable for Henty (Mrs Child) the most extraordimiry remark that there are no jobs available. Of course, I could remind members of the Opposition of how effective their policies were in the job area. 25 August 1981 REPRESENTATIVES 757 ANSWERS TO QUESTIONS

The following answers to questions were circulated:

Leaching of Ore Bodies
(Question No. 589)
Mr Holding asked the Minister for Home Affairs and Environment, upon notice, on 25 February 1981:
(I) Has his Department or any other Commonwealth department or authorities made any examination of (a) the general environmental impact of the process of leaching of ore bodies to obtain minerals and (b) the specific environmental impact of the leaching process if used to recover uranium from the Beverley uranium prosl'ect in South Australia.
(2) If so, what was the nature of this examination giving (a) the Commonwealth departments or authorities concerned and (b) the names, substantive gradings, salaries and qualifications of the specific personnel involved.
(3) Did any examination involve (a).scientific literature reviews and (b) actual physical testing of the process; if so, what are the details.
Mr Wilson-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
(I) (a) I have been advised that the CSIRO is collecting data relevant to the environmental assessment of the leaching process on ore bodies. My Department has recently examined in situ leach mining in relation to the proposed Honeymoon Uranium Project in South Australia.
(b) The specific environmental impacts of the leaching process if used to recover uranium from the Beverley uranium proposal will be examined under the provisions of the Environment Protection (Impact of Proposals) Act.
(2) The proposed Honeymoon Uranium Project was examined through the preparation of an environmental impact statement by Mines Administration Pty Ltd in accordance with the Administrative Procedures under the Environment Protection (Impact of Proposals) Act.
(a) The following Commonwealth instrumentalities were consulted:
Australian Atomic Energy Commission Australian Heritage Commission Australian Radiation Laboratory Bureau of Mineral Resources Department of Aboriginal Affairs Department of Health Department of National Development and Energy Uranium Advisory Council

National Semiconductor Corporation
(Ql!estion No. 2092)
Mrs Kelly asked the Minister for the Capital Territory, upon notice, on 6 May 1981:
(I) Will he provide a list of the types of jobs that will become available to residents of the Australian Capital Territory from the implementation of the National Semiconductor project and the approximate numbers involved in each type of job.
(2) What assurances have been given by National Semiconductor Corporation of the numbers of jobs that will be available for local persons.
.Mr Hodgman-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
(I) It is not possible to provide detailed lists of the types and numbers of jobs which will be generated by the National Semiconductor project. Further information is likely to become available during the course of the feasibility study. At present it is expected that the manufacturing plant itself will employ from 1,150-1,250 persons.
Approximately 20 per cent of the positions created will represent highly skilled jobs requiring the equivalent of tertiary qualifications in science and engineering. ApJ?foximately 30 per cent will comprise positions requiring technical or trade qualifications and approximately 50 per cent will comprise unskille<! and semi-skilled positions. This represents a broad, general classification and will be subject to variation when planning for the project reaches a more advanced stage.
Construction of the project will create additional jobs as will the multiplier effects on the rest of the Australian Capital Territory economy. -In addition, experience in centres of high technology in ()ther countries indicates that other private enterprise developments of a related nature are likely to be attracted to the Australian Capital Teritory once the NATSEMI project commences.
(2) NATSEMI has not given assurances on jobs for locals. However, the magnitude of the project is. such that a favourable impact on employment opportunities in the Australian Capital Territory will occur. Officials are curently examining the Govern~ent's position.on many issues associated with the staffing of the plant and these include the question of making employment opportunities available for disadvantaged groups including the disabled and the long term young unemployed. These matters will be pursued with the company during negotiations following the completion of the feasibility study.
Shopping Hours: Australian Capital Territory
(Question No. 2094)
Mrs Kelly asked the Minister for the Capital Territory, upon notice, oi16 May 1981:
(I) Why was action taken to deregulate shopping hours in the Australian Capital Territory.
(2) What studies were done prior to this decision to evaluate its likely effects.
(3) Were small business owners consulted.
(4) Were the recommendations of the Members of the House of Assembly considered.
(5) Were the views of employees (lrganisations considered.

760 REPRESENTATIYES 25 August 1981

Answers to Questions

(6) Will estimates of the increased cost of goods resulting from de-regulation of shopping hours be made available to the public; if so when.
Mr Hodgman-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
(I) The decision to deregulate shopping hours in the Australian Capital Territory was taken as part of the Ministerial Review of Commonwealth Functions and conforms with the Government's philosophy of minimising direct involvement by Government in the activities of the private sector.
(2) In recent years the Department of the Capital Territory has undertaken detailed research into the problem of trading hours in Canberra. Further research on the question of the regulation of trading hours has been undertaken by employer and employee organisations and was also the subject of a recent report by the Bureau of Industry Economics.
(3), (4) & (5) Representatives of employees, employers and small businesses have been consulted by the Department of the Capital Territory during consideration of this issue over recent years.
Neither these organisations nor the Australian Capital Territory House of Assembly were consulted in the context of the Review of Commonwealth Functions.
However, officers of my Department have, at my request, had further discussions with groups representing employers, employees and small businesses on the question of implementation of the decision.
I have supported the establishment of a consultative committee comprising representatives of interested groups to monitor the effects of de-regulating trading hours in the Australian Capital Territory.
The establishment of this committee however has been overtaken by my undertaking not to recommend commencement of the legislation to repeal the Trading Hours Ordinance 1962 until the matter has been considered by the Joint Parliamentary Committee on the Australian Capital Territory.
(6) Information about price levels of goods will be published in the normal way by the Australian Bureau of Statistics.

(5) What is the current value of the Belconnen Mall complex.
Mr Hodgman-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:

(I) Arrangements are being made to sell th~ Belconnen Mall as soon as possible.
(2) The decision to sell the Mall was made ,as part of the Review of Commonwealth Functions. The issue of different management plans did not arise at that time.
(3) The Government will take into account normal commercial considerations involved in such a sale as well as factors relevant to the public interest.
(4) The proposal that small business owners form a body corporate to lease and manage the Mall has been raised with me. I have had discussions with relevant groups and will give this proposal, and others, careful consideration.
(5) It would be premature to anticipate a value for the Belconnen Mall at this stage. The process of sale will determine a market value for the complex.

Milk Authority and Showground Trust, Australian Capital Territory

Mr Hodgman-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:

Service Housing: Darwin
(Question No. 2243)

Mr Killen-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:

Commonwealth Development Bank
(Question No. 2290)
Mr Barry Jones asked the Treasurer, upon notice, on 14 May 1981:
What (a) amount and (b) percentage of Commonwealth Development Bank lending has been placed in each State and Territory in each of the last five years and what formula was used to determine the distribution in each case.
Mr Howard-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
The Managing Director of the Commonwealth Banking Corporation has advised that figures on the distribution of Commonwealth Development Bank lending as between the States and the Territories are not made available because of possible misinterpretation. As a supplementary lender, the Development Bank relies largely on its agent banks for acceptance and submission of applications for finance. Thus, the elltent to which its facilities are availed of in a particular State or Territory depends substantially on the level of referrals from the various trading banks. Comparison of the levels of approvals in dilferent States or Territories would therefore be inappropriate and could be misleading. Moreover, the problem could be complicated by the small number of loan approvals encompassed by some of those figures and the consequent implications for protecting traditional banker/customer confidentiality. It is for these reasons that the Development Bank does not make available statistics relating to lending in an individual State or Territory.

Cost ofLhe-in Hospital Facilities
(Question N". 2363)
Dr Blewett asked the Minister for Health, upon notice, on 28 May 1981:
What would be the estimated usage and cost if the Commonwealth allowed or supported a benefit to be paid for charges levied on mothers who wish to live in with their hospitalised child.
Mr MacKellar--The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows: '
All State and Territory health authorities have advised that limited live-in facilities for parents of hospitalised children may be provided where circumstances require it and such accommodation is available at the time. However, in some States live-in accommodation is limited to particular hospitals.
At the present time, charges for accommodation vary between the States/Territory viz:
New South Wales-$4 per night Victoria-$5 per night (this can be varied) Queensland-$6 per night (Brisbane Royal Children's Hospital only) South Australia-ranges to $6 per night Western Australia-$I 0 per night Tasmania'-no charge Northern Territory-no charge Australian Capital Territory-$3 per night.
In some hospitals the charges are all inclusive and in others meals are elltra., Where charges are raised they are generally met by parents.
Detailed information is not available regarding the extent of utilisation, but, from that provided by the States, it does not appear that extensive use is made of this type of facility. From the limited information available, it is not possible to'determine accurately the likely cost to the Commonwealth of any benefit which might be paid to parents who may wish to live in with a hospitalised child.

Work Value of Household Work

(Questi9n No. 2365)

Mr Barry Jones asked the Treasurer, upon notice, on 28 May I 981 :

(I) Is it a fact that the National Accounts do not measure

the economic value of work performed within the home,

especially by housewives.

'

(2) Has his attention been drawn to the .study published by
Statistics Canada entitled 'Estimating the work value of household work in Canada by Oli Hawrylyshyn.

(3) Will the Government provide funds to the Australian
Bureau of Statistics to conduct a time use study among house-
holds to determine the value of household work in Australia and take steps to end the statistical discrimination involved in ignoring it when calculating the national accounts.

Mr Howard-The answer to the honourable member'squestion is as follows:

Answers to Questions

2S August 1981 REPRESENTATIVES 763

(I) Yes.
(2) Yes.
(3) The suggested study of time use in households is considered by the Australian Statistician to be of lower priority than other topics For household surveys, such as Family relationships, income studies, health conditions and household expenditure patterns. In any case, such a study would not determine the value of work done within households. Even if it were decided For some purposes to accept as a guide the value of services carried out in a market situation, relating the value of activities within households to the value of activities in a market situation would be subject to wide variations depending on purely subjective judgements.
The definitions of production and related national accounting aggregates which are used to construct the Australian national accounts are consistent with those recommeded in the United Nations publication 'A System of National Accounts' which is the internationally accepted national accounting standard. The Statistician is not aware of any country which currently includes the value of household work in its official national accounts.

East Timor
(Question No. 2387)
Dr Everingham asked the Minister for Foreign Affairs, upon notice, on 3 June 1981:
( I) Did Australian observers attend el(ercises by 10,000 Indonesian troops in East Timor in March 1981.
(2) Is he able to say whether (a) 18,000 troops are engaged in a clean-up offensive to wipe out Fretilin dissenters, (b) 5000 political prisoners are confined to Atauro Island and (c) army atrocities are continuing in East Timor.
(3) Does Australia support the Portuguese proposal for a United Nations Commission to negotiate a peaceFul settlement in East Timor despite Indonesia's opposition; if not, why not.
Mr Street-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
(I) The Australian Defence Attache, together with a number of military attaches From other countries resident in

Jakarta, observed a recent major Indonesian joint exercise which involved the development of some 35,000 men together with naval ships and aircraft, in eastern Indonesia. The exercise was held From 18 March to I April 1981 in three separate exercise locations: Timor, Maluku and Irian Jaya.
(2) (a) Fretilin guerrilla remnants are reported to be still actively hostile towards the authorities in the Indonesian Province of East Timor. It is For the Indonesian Government to decide how to deal with this threat to security there.
.(b) The Government is aware of press reports that 5,000 prisioners are being held on Atauro Island but has no inFormation to substantiate this allegation.
(c) The Government is aware of recent reports of Indonesian army atrocities in East Timor, but has no evidence to substantiate them. The Australian Government's position on violations of internationally-accepted standards of human rights is of course well known. The Indonesian Government is aware of Australia's views.
(3) The Government is closely watching developments relating to the Portuguese proposal. The proposal is however in the early stages of its development. In considering its approach, the Government will need to take account of the attitudes of both the Indonesian and Portuguese Governments.

National Disaster Relief (Health) Committee: Survey of Medical Practitioners
(Question No. 2493)
Dr Klugman asked the Minister for Health, upon notice, on SJune 1981:

(1) Has the National Disaster RelieF (Health) Committee recently completed a survey of medical practitioners. '

(2) If so, how many owned a kit of surgical instruments with which, in a national emergency, they could perform a (a) craniotomy, (b) amputation of the limbs and (c)
thoracotomy.

(3) Is the Committee satisfied with the result of this survey.

Mr MacKellar-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:

(I) The National Disaster Relief (Health) Committee maintains a Register of Medical Practitioners in Australia for
possible national emergency relieF purposes. The Register has existe!,j since 1950 and is being regularly updated. All practising doctors are approached, usually every three years, to vol-
untarily submit information for incorporation into the
Register.

(2) Of nearly 24,000 practitioners surveyed, 2,111 doctors
have indicated that they possess a kit of surgical instruments. The quantity of kits for purposes listed in the honourable member's question are-

(a) Craniotomy-227 (b) Amputation of the limbs-2,16 (c) Thoracotomy-I 55

(The remainder are available For general surgery use, inc,1ud-,

ing laparotomy.)

,

(3)' Whilst the current level of co-operation, with over 80

per cent of practising doctors supplying the information

requested, Is encouraging, further improvement in the near

future is expected. Update procedures have recently been

reviewed and during the last quarter oFthisyear all practisi,ng

doctors from whom information has not been received will be

specifically approached.

Answers to Questhms

Trade Practices Commission Investigation of Stockbroking Industry
(Question No. 2610)
Mr Hurford asked the Minister for Business and Consumer Affairs, upon notice, on 10 June 1981:
(I) Is it a fact that, despite the decisions taken at a recent meeting of the Council of Ministers, the Trade Practices Commission investigation into the stockbroking industry is still iIi a state of limbo.
(2) Will action be taken to respond to criticism from, among others, the Merchant Bankers Association, that the regulatory distinctions currently made by the Government between the activities of merchant bankers and stockbrokers are discriminatory; if so, what action.
(3) Has his attention been drawn to further criticism from the Managing Director of BT Australia Limited who described the decision to halt the Commission's investigation of stockbrokers as one which smacked of delaying tactics by the Government under lobbying pressure from the securities industry to allow the continuation of the existing exorbitant fee scales and club membership of the stockbroking industry.
. (4) If so, is allowing these criticisms to go unanswered unfair to the stockbroking profession and does it deserve an objective assessment of its functions and methods.
(5) Was a deCision taken at a recent meeting of the Council of Ministers that all changes to the new legislative package governing company and security legislation must be passed by a unanimous vote of the Council.
(6) Is it also a fact that the New South Wales Government has stated opposition to placing the stockbroking industry under the auspices of the National Companies and Securities Commission.
(7) If so, then if the industry is to be effectively examined and audited to ensure the public interest is being served will he again give the Trade Practices Commission authority to proceed with its investigations.
Mr Moore-The answer to the honourable member's question is as foIlows:
As I announced on 5 August 1981 the Government has decided that the Trade Practices Commission will retain responsibility for the competition provisions of the Trade Practices Act insofar as they apply to stock exchanges.
Commonwealth Accommodation and Catering Services Ltd
(Question No. 2619)
Mr Barry Jones asked the Minister for Administrative Services, upon notice, on 10 June 1981:
(I) Following the decision announced in the ministerial statement on the review of Commonwealth Functions (Hansard, 30 April 1981, page 1841) with respect to the recommended transfer of certain functions performed by Commonwealth Accommodation and Catering Services (CACS Ltd) to private enterprise, is it the Government's intention to wind up the activities of CACS Ltd altogether; if so, when will this occur.
(2) What are the estimated savings involved as a result of the transfer of the operation of migrant centres and other operations from CACS Ltd to private enterprise and how are these savings made up; if no savings are involved, what is the estimated cost in transferring these functions.
(3) Will the transfer involve additional public servants over and above those already involved in monitoring the operations

to be transferred to private industry; if so, how many and at what cost.
(4) Was the Government approached by a particular organisation prior to reaching its decision with an offer to take over all or some of the functions currently being performed by CACS Ltd and were discussions held between this organisation and departmental officers at that time.
(5) If so, 'what information regarding the structure and financial operations of CACS Ltd, including the arrangement with the Commonwealth, was given to that organisation.
(6) Did that organisation submit a proposal to his Department or the Committee of Re,view of Commonwealth Functions for the operation of any of the functions being performed by CACS Ltd; if so, on what basis was this proposal made.
(7) Has any subsequent contact been made or discussions held between the Government and that organisation following the handing down of the recommendations; if so, on what basis.
(8) Have any other private enterprise organisations been contacted or have they contacted the Government regarding the takeover of some or all of the functions ofCACS Ltd; ifso, what (a) financial or (b) other information has been given to them
(9) Was the information given to these organisations identical to that given to the organisation referred to in part (4).
Mr Newman-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
(I) The functions of CACS Ltd fall into four groups: migrant centres, non-departmental food (and other) services, guest houses for public servants in the Australian Capital Territory, and departmental food services. As indicated in the Prime Minister's statement of 30 April 1981, the first two functions are to be offered or transferred to the private sector; one guest house is to be placed on the market and the future of the others reviewed; and departmental food services are to be reviewed. As no final decisions have been reached on transferring all these functions to the private sector, neither has any final decision been reached on the future of CACS Ltd.
(2) In advance of the activities being advertised for transfer, and offers being received, it is not possible to say what savings or costs will result.
(3) See answer to (2). Any additional public servants required are likely to be offset by staff savings in the present CACS Ltd management.
(4) An approach was made to my Department by Nationwide Food Service Pty Ltd on 28 September 1979.
(5) The Company was given such information on CACS Ltd as was publicly available, including the 1978-79 CACS Ltd Annual Report and relevant extracts from the 1979-80 Estimates Explanation.
(6) On 28 April 1980, Nationwide Food Service Pty Ltd submitted a proposal to manage the CACS Ltd food services on the basis that it could achieve savings fpr the Government.
(7) Following the Prime Minister's statement of 30 April 1981, my Department notified Nationwide Food Service Pty Ltd of the non-departmental food services to be transferred to the private sector and that the operation of departmental food services was still under review.
(8) I am advised that my Department has not initiated contact with any private enterprise organisations, either before or after the Review of Commonwealth Functions, regarding the takeover of some or all the functions of CACS Ltd. Enquiries have been received from a number of organisations and have been handled in a similar manner to those received from Nationwide Food Service Pty Ltd. My Department has been

carerul to ensure that no private operator has gained any unrair advantage over other prospective tenderers.
(9) See answer to (8).

(Question No. 2621)
Dr Klugman asked the Minister Assisting the Prime Minister, upon notice, on 10 June 1981:
What was the saving in public service salaries and wages resulting rrom industrial disputes in each year rrom 1975-76 and what is the estimated saving ror 1980-81

Mr Viner-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
I am inrormed that details or the saving in public service salaries and wages resulting rrom industrial disputes ror each year since 1975-76 are not readily available.
In order to provide the inrormation sought, examination or
personnel records held by each department would be necessary. Allocation or the resources needed to undertake this task is not considered warranted.
